<p><b>Air Berlin PLC &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs KG</b> (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">FWB</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.boerse-frankfurt.de/en/equities/search/result?name_isin_wkn=AB1">AB1</a>), branded as <b>airberlin</b> or <b>airberlin.com</b>, is <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>'s second-largest <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_airlines_in_Europe" title="List of largest airlines in Europe">Europe's seventh-largest airline</a> in terms of passengers carried.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It maintains hubs at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-www.anna.aero_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.anna.aero-4">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf Airport</a> and serves 12 German cities as well as destinations in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.</p>
<p>Air Berlin is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> alliance, and owns the subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a> in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> while the sale of its 49% stake <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">NIKI</a> to <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> was announced in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale-5">[5]</a></sup> It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a>. <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> is the largest shareholder, having increased its shareholding to 29.21% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-2012AR_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012AR-6">[6]</a></sup> Air Berlin is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf" title="Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf">Charlottenburg-Wilmersdorf</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 August 2017 Air Berlin stated it was filing for insolvency, but that flights would continue, in part thanks to a loan provided by the <a href="/wiki/German_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="German Government">German Government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1978-1990:_American_charter_airline_in_West_Berlin">1978-1990: American <a href="/wiki/Charter_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter airline">charter airline</a> in West Berlin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1978-1990: American charter airline in West Berlin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft">

The Original Air Berlin USA logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Originally registered as <b>Air Berlin USA</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-10">[10]</a></sup> the company was founded in 1978 as a wholly owned subsidiary of Lelco, an American agricultural enterprise headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-10">[10]</a></sup> to operate charter flights on behalf of German tour operators from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a>, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> holiday resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg91_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg91-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The co-founders of Air Berlin USA were:</p>
<ul>
<li>Kim Lundgren, a former Berlin-based <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">flight engineer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>;</li>
<li>John MacDonald, a former station manager of United States supplemental<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[nb 1]</a></sup> and charter airline <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Airways" title="Saturn Airways">Saturn Airways</a> at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport" title="Berlin Tempelhof Airport">Berlin Tempelhof Airport</a> in the 1960s and subsequent general manager Europe and <a href="/wiki/Vice_president" title="Vice president">vice president</a> at the Berlin Tegel Airport base of the former United States supplemental carrier and charter airline <a href="/wiki/Modern_Air_Transport" title="Modern Air Transport">Modern Air</a> from 1968 until 1974;</li>
<li>Mort Beyer, Modern Air's <a href="/wiki/Executive_vice_president" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive vice president">executive vice president</a> from 1967 until 1971 as well as the airline's <a href="/wiki/President_(corporate_title)" title="President (corporate title)">president</a> and vice president of the National Air Carrier Association<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[nb 2]</a></sup> in 1971 and founder of United States aviation consultancy Avmark.<sup id="cite_ref-DT_ABStartUp_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT_ABStartUp-14">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Lelco was the agriculture business of Kim Lundgren's family in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-DT_ABStartUp_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT_ABStartUp-14">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a United States airline, Air Berlin was able to access the <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> airline market. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Berlin's special political status meant that the <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin_Air_Corridor" title="West Berlin Air Corridor">air corridors</a> into and out of Tegel Airport could only be used by airlines registered in France, the United Kingdom or the United States. The airline's headquarters were initially at Tegel Airport. Leonard Lundgren was the first chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-fg80_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg80-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the company was issued an <a href="/wiki/Air_Operator%27s_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Operator's Certificate">airline licence</a> and acquired two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a> jet airliners previously owned by <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">Trans World Airlines</a>, Air Berlin USA commenced revenue services on 28 April 1979 with a flight from Berlin-Tegel to <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fg79_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg79-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-19">[17]</a></sup> Plans were made to start long-haul flights on West Berlin-<a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>-<a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> routes,<sup id="cite_ref-fg79_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg79-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timetable81_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timetable81-20">[18]</a></sup> in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Air_Florida" title="Air Florida">Air Florida</a> (an agreement to that effect had been signed in February 1979).<sup id="cite_ref-fg81_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg81-21">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1980, the Air Berlin USA fleet grew to include the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_City_Jet" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing City Jet">Boeing 737-200</a>, when two aircraft of that type were leased from Air Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-22">[20]</a></sup> In 1981, Air Berlin USA was continuing to operate scheduled transatlantic Boeing 707 service on a weekly routing of Berlin <a href="/wiki/Tegel_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Tegel Airport">Tegel Airport</a> - Brussels - <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> however, by 1982, the 707s had been phased out, and during most of the 1980s, Air Berlin USA operated only a single 737-200<sup id="cite_ref-fg84_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg84-24">[22]</a></sup> or (from 1986) a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">737-300</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg89_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg89-25">[23]</a></sup> In 1990 and 1991, two modern <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">Boeing 737-400s</a> were also placed into service.<sup id="cite_ref-fg91_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg91-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg90_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg90-26">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990-2000:_New_owners_and_the_start_of_low-cost_flights">1990-2000: New owners and the start of low-cost flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1990-2000: New owners and the start of low-cost flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> led to significant changes to the Berlin aviation market, since German airlines gained access to the city. In 1991, Air Berlin (which had 90 employees at the time)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> was bought by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joachim_Hunold&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joachim Hunold (page does not exist)">Joachim Hunold</a> (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joachim_Hunold" class="extiw" title="de:Joachim Hunold">de</a>), a former sales and marketing director with <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU International</a>, and restructured as <b>Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Gesellschaft_mit_beschr%C3%A4nkter_Haftung" title="Gesellschaft mit beschränkter Haftung">GmbH</a> &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs <a href="/wiki/Kommanditgesellschaft" title="Kommanditgesellschaft">KG</a></b>, a German-registered company.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-19">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1992_737_order_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1992_737_order-28">[26]</a></sup> Following an order for ten <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a>, Air Berlin grew and by 1999, the fleet comprised twelve aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-fg99_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg99-29">[27]</a></sup> In 2001, Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/Hapag-Lloyd_Flug" title="Hapag-Lloyd Flug">Hapag-Lloyd Flug</a> became the first airlines in the world to have their Boeing 737-800s fitted with <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">blended winglets</a>, wingtip devices that are intended to improve <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-winglets_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winglets-30">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin introduced scheduled flights (which could be booked directly with the airline rather than via a tour operator) in 1997, initially linking a number of secondary German airports to Majorca.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-19">[17]</a></sup> By 2002, 35 percent of Air Berlin's tickets were sold directly.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29-31">[29]</a></sup> In the same year, the route network grew to include destinations other than typical holiday resorts: Low-fare flights to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> started. They were marketed as <i>City Shuttle</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-19">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29-31">[29]</a></sup> Besides Berlin-Tegel, these routes were opened at six German airports (<a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="Düsseldorf Airport">Düsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster_Osnabr%C3%BCck_International_Airport" title="Münster Osnabrück International Airport">Münster/Osnabrück</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paderborn_Lippstadt_Airport" title="Paderborn Lippstadt Airport">Paderborn/Lippstadt</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_.281.29_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_.281.29-32">[30]</a></sup> that until then had not been served by one of the rising European low-cost carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_.282.29-31">[29]</a></sup> In what later would become a hallmark for Air Berlin as a "semi-low cost carrier", the airline offered complimentary meals and seat reservations.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_lowcost_expansion_.281.29_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_lowcost_expansion_.281.29-32">[30]</a></sup> This was something its competitors <a href="/wiki/Buzz_(airline)" title="Buzz (airline)">Buzz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hapag-Lloyd_Express" title="Hapag-Lloyd Express">Hapag-Lloyd Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Express" title="Virgin Express">Virgin Express</a> did not do.</p>
<h3><span id="2000-2006:_Becoming_Germany’s_second-largest_airline"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000-2006:_Becoming_Germany.E2.80.99s_second-largest_airline">2000-2006: Becoming Germany’s second-largest airline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2000-2006: Becoming Germany’s second-largest airline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2001, the delivery flight of Boeing 737-800 fitted with winglets set a record: the aircraft with the registration code D-ABBC flew 8,345 kilometres non-stop from Seattle (BFI), USA to Berlin (TXL), Germany in 9 hours, 10 minutes.</p>
<p>In January 2004, Air Berlin announced it would cooperate with <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>, a Vienna-based airline.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_history_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_history-19">[17]</a></sup> As part of the deal, Air Berlin took a 24% stake in Niki.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/220px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" width="220" height="61" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/330px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png/440px-Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="207" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Old_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The old Air Berlin logo used from 1986 until 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, Air Berlin signed a partnership agreement with <a href="/wiki/Germania_(airline)" title="Germania (airline)">Germania</a>. As part of the deal, Air Berlin leased some of Germania's aircraft and crew, and Germania became almost exclusively a charter airline. Plans were made for Germania to be associated with Air Berlin under a management contract. However, the contract was not signed. At the beginning of March 2008 Germania’s joint owners could not reach agreement on the takeover by Air Berlin, so Germania remained an independent airline. A joint Air Berlin/Germania subsidiary dubbed <i>Air Zürich</i> and planned to be based at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> was proposed in 2005, but did not materialize.</p>
<p>In 2005 the Group reorganised its corporate structure. It established Air Berlin plc (registered in England) into which it reversed Air Berlin GmbH &amp; Co. Luftverkehrs KG and subsidiaries.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> It was suggested that the reason for the group to establish a UK-based PLC instead a German-based AG was to avoid the need to have a supervisory board and employee representation as required by the German law of <i>Mitbestimmung</i> or <a href="/wiki/Co-determination" title="Co-determination">co-determination</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">went public</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Stock_Exchange" title="Frankfurt Stock Exchange">Frankfurt Stock Exchange</a>. Originally scheduled for 5 May 2006, the IPO was postponed to 11 May 2006. The company said the delay was due to rises in fuel costs and other market pressures limiting investor demand. It reduced the initial share-price range from 15.0–17.5 <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a> to 11.5–14.5 euros. The stock opened at €12.0, selling a total of 42.5 million shares. Of these, 19.6 million were new shares increasing capital in the company, and the remainder to repay loans extended by the original shareholders and invested in the company earlier in 2006. After the IPO, the company claimed to have over 400 million euros in cash to fund further expansion, including aircraft purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2006, Air Berlin acquired German domestic airline <a href="/wiki/DBA_(airline)" title="DBA (airline)">dba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dba_takeover_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dba_takeover-36">[34]</a></sup> Flight operations at dba were continued as a fully owned subsidiary of Air Berlin until 14 November 2008, when the dba brand was discontinued due to staff strikes (dba staff were subsequently offered positions with Air Berlin).</p>
<p>On 28 November 2006, Air Berlin ordered 60 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-800</a> aircraft,<sup id="cite_ref-boeing_order_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boeing_order-37">[35]</a></sup> and 15 smaller <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700</a> aircraft. The combined value of the 75 aircraft was 5.1 billion <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">dollars</a> (based on list prices at the time.) Delivery of the aircraft started in 2007. All of these aircraft were equipped with blended <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device" title="Wingtip device">winglets</a>, to significantly improve fuel efficiency.</p>
<h3><span id="2007-2012:_Takeovers,_expansion_and_new_alliances"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007-2012:_Takeovers.2C_expansion_and_new_alliances">2007-2012: Takeovers, expansion and new alliances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2007-2012: Takeovers, expansion and new alliances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-76Q,_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/220px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/330px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg/440px-Boeing_737-76Q%2C_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="718" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_737-76Q,_Air_Berlin_AN0775825.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In 2005, one of Air Berlin's <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700s</a> featured a special livery promoting Boeing's <i><a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Dreamliner</a></i> program.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/220px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/330px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg/440px-Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Airbus_A330-200_Prasertwit-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Following the takeover of <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU</a> in 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-200">Airbus A330-200</a> <i>(pictured)</i> became part of Air Berlin's fleet. This long-haul aircraft enabled the airline to start flying to intercontinental destinations like <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> (as in this case, depicting an approach to <a href="/wiki/Suvarnabhumi_Airport" title="Suvarnabhumi Airport">Suvarnabhumi Airport</a> in 2008).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2007, Air Berlin took over German leisure airline <a href="/wiki/LTU_International" title="LTU International">LTU</a>, gaining access to the long-haul market and becoming the fourth-largest airline group in Europe in terms of passenger traffic. This deal led to the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330</a> aircraft into Air Berlin's fleet. The merger of the LTU operations, aircraft and crew was completed on 1 May 2009, when the LTU brand was discontinued.</p>
<p>On 7 July 2007, Air Berlin announced an order for 25 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-8 Dreamliner</a> longhaul aircraft, with further options and purchase rights.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> Three additional aircraft of this type will be leased from <a href="/wiki/International_Lease_Finance_Corporation" title="International Lease Finance Corporation">ILFC</a>.</p>
<p>On 21 August 2007, Air Berlin acquired a 49 percent shareholding in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> charter airline <a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a>, the remainder being owned by tour operator Hotelplan.<sup id="cite_ref-DK_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DK-39">[37]</a></sup> Following the deal, Belair's long-haul business was terminated, and the fleet replaced by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320 family</a> aircraft operating scheduled flights on behalf of Air Berlin as well as charter flights for Hotelplan.</p>
<p>On 20 September 2007, Air Berlin announced it intended to buy its direct competitor <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> in a deal that envisaged Condor's owner, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group" title="Thomas Cook Group">Thomas Cook Group</a>, taking a 30% stake in Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-condor_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-condor-40">[38]</a></sup> A variety of considerations, including the <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis" title="2000s energy crisis">rapidly increasing price of jet fuel</a>, led to the abandonment of the deal in July 2008.</p>
<p>In January 2008 Air Berlin introduced a new logo and corporate design. The logo is a white oval shape on a red background (suggesting an aircraft window) where the letter “a” is a white circle and two white stylised wings. The text "Air Berlin" in the logo is now in lower case and written as one word. Sometimes the slogan “Your Airline” also features as part of the logo.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2008, CEO Joachim Hunold offended <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan language</a> speakers, when he claimed<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> in an article included in Air Berlin's <a href="/wiki/Inflight_magazine" title="Inflight magazine">inflight magazine</a> that the government of the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> was trying to impose the use of <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> on Air Berlin flights from and to <a href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>. He claimed that Air Berlin was an international airline and was not obliged to use Catalan. Hunold went on to criticise the language policy in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> and the Balearic Islands, claiming that at the time many children could not speak any Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> The Balearic Islands' President, Francesc Antich, explained that his government had simply sent a letter to encourage airlines operating in the Balearic Islands to include Catalan among the languages used for onboard announcements.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 June of the same year, Air Berlin announced that it would reduce its long-haul services by 13 percent, as well as cut 10 percent of services in the domestic market in an effort to increase profitability.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2008, Air Berlin confirmed merger talks with competitor TUIfly, but added it was speaking with all parties. Air Berlin had, until 2007, been flying many code-share TUI flights. At the end of March 2009, Air Berlin PLC and TUI Travel PLC signed a deal by which their German flight businesses were to operate a long-term strategic alliance. Originally, each company was to take a 19.9% stake in the other and the German cartel authorities were petitioned for approval. After the Bundeskartellamt expressed concerns, the cross ownership plan was not implemented. Instead, TUI Travel PLC purchased a 9.9% stake in Air Berlin PLC using a capital increase at a subsidiary to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2009 Air Berlin started cooperating with <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a>, China’s fourth-largest airline. The airlines jointly market flights between <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>. The code-share flights are sold on a reciprocal basis and operated under the relevant airline’s own flight number.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of March 2009, a strategic partnership agreement with <a href="/wiki/TUI_Travel" title="TUI Travel">TUI Travel</a> was signed, with Air Berlin and its direct competitor <a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> purchasing 19.9 percent of the other's shares.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> Following the deal, Air Berlin took over all German domestic TUIfly routes, as well as those to <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. Also, all of Tuifly's <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737-700</a> aircraft were added to Air Berlin's fleet. Further route changes will see TUIfly abandoning all scheduled flights and relying exclusively on the charter business.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2009, ESAS Holding A.S., a Turkish company bought approximately 15 per cent of the voting shares in Air Berlin, to which the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Cartel_Office" title="Federal Cartel Office">German competition regulator</a> had no objections.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 September 2009, Air Berlin announced it would cooperate with <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a>, allowing its customers access to more destinations and flights to and within <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Codeshare" class="mw-redirect" title="Codeshare">codeshare</a>-like basis.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2009, Air Berlin added Hartmut Mehdorn to the board of directors after his retirement at Deutsche Bahn.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2009 Air Berlin started cooperating with <a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Airways" title="Bangkok Airways">Bangkok Airways</a>. Bangkok Airways flights can be booked on a codeshare basis by Air Berlin customers.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable floatleft">

</tr>
<tr>

</tr>
<tr>

<td align="right">100&#160;%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a></td>
<td align="right">100&#160;%</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In April 2010 Air Berlin expanded its codeshare arrangements with Russia’s <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">S7 Airlines</a>. Air Berlin and S7 Airlines had been cooperating since October 2008. New services include codeshare flights via Moscow to destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perm" title="Perm">Perm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rostov" title="Rostov">Rostov</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2010, Air Berlin announced an increase in its shareholding in the Austrian airline <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>. Following the fulfilment of the required conditions, the agreements notarized on 17 February 2010 have been implemented. Air Berlin indirectly acquired 25.9% of the shares in Niki from Privatstiftung Lauda (private Lauda foundation) and in doing so increased its current shareholding in Niki from 24% to 49.9%. In connection with the increase of its shareholding, Air Berlin will grant the private Lauda foundation a 40.5 million-euro loan. The private foundation has the option to repay the loan in three years with cash or through the transfer of the remaining 50.1% of Niki's shares.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D-ABMC_(8629266400)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-D-ABMC_%288629266400%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4249" data-file-height="2833" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D-ABMC_(8629266400)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Since becoming a member of <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a>, several Air Berlin aircraft display the global airline alliance's logo, as seen on this <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_Air_Berlin_JP6900509.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a> on <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> in 2010, featuring a livery variant using the "Air Berlin" titles on the tail prior to the introduction of the current logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In July 2010, it was also announced that Air Berlin would join <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a>, the global <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> In preparation for joining the alliance, Air Berlin began to offer flights under codeshare agreements with <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a>, starting with the 2010/2011 winter schedule. Its cooperation with American Airlines means that Air Berlin passengers gain access to the American market whilst it also offers codeshare flights with Finnair to Helsinki and within Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin founded Follow Me Entertainment GmbH in September 2010 as a joint venture with kick-media ag. This joint venture company markets image and sound media, books, games as well as events, concerts, tournaments and sponsoring.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The foundations were laid for the first maintenance hangar at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a> (BER) on 21 March 2011. Air Berlin, which will share use of the hangar with Germania when the airport is opened, has doubled Air Berlin Technik's maintenance capacity at its Berlin site.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 1 April 2011 Air Berlin completed the integration of LTU which it took over in August 2007. There is now a single flight schedule and all Air Berlin Group technical services have been merged into a new company called airberlin technik GmbH.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> Also in April 2011 Air Berlin underlined the importance of its Düsseldorf hub by creating a new position of North-Rhine Westphalia Regional Director. It also added new routes, more frequent flights and additional long-haul flights from Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 June 2011, Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> reached a codeshare agreement covering some flights within Europe, starting from 5 July 2011. The agreement applies to flights to over 40 European destinations served by the two airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>CEO Joachim Hunold resigned from his position on 1 September 2011 and was succeeded by the former CEO of Deutsche Bahn AG, Hartmut Mehdorn, who led the company on an interim basis until January 2013. From January 2013 Wolfgang Prock-Schauer took over the position of CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin has cooperated with the Italian airline Meridiana since September 2011, and has offered flights since 30 October 2011 with Meridiana between Italy and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2011 Air Berlin and <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a> launched <i>Air Berlin Turkey</i>, aiming at the charter market between Germany and Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a> is the largest private airline company in Turkey and is 16.5% owned by ESAS Holding AS.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> involved in Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> The new airline was absorbed into Pegasus Airlines on 31 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 3rd quarter of 2011, the turnover of the company amounted to 1.4 billion euros, an increase of 11%. However operating profit decreased by almost to 50%, around 97 million euros. As a result, a new bond to raise additional capital was issued.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> In November 2011, a marketing campaign was launched and further preparations to join the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">oneworld</a> airline alliance were made.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2011 Air Berlin took over the remaining 50.1% stake in NIKI in the repayment of a loan and is now the sole owner of the company. The brand name is to be retained and Niki Lauda was given a position on the board of Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin announced on 19 December 2011 that the Abu Dhabi airline Etihad Airways had increased its share of Air Berlin from 2.99% to 29.1%, for a sum of 73 million euros, immediately making Etihad the company's largest shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals-72">[70]</a></sup> The deal supplied more cash to Air Berlin, and provided Etihad access to Air Berlin's European network.<sup id="cite_ref-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folgen_des_Etihad-Berlin-Deals-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin became a full member of Oneworld on 20 March 2012, a move that was originally announced on 2 February 2012. Austrian airline NIKI, which is also part of the Air Berlin group, joined Oneworld as an affiliate member on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012-2015:_Restructuring_amid_continuing_losses">2012-2015: Restructuring amid continuing losses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012-2015: Restructuring amid continuing losses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/220px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/330px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg/440px-Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airberlin_aircraft_at_Berlin_Tegel_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Air Berlin aircraft at Terminal C of <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Berlin Tegel Airport</a> in September 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Air Berlin has been flying seven times a week non-stop from Berlin to Abu Dhabi since January 2012. The new service is also the start of the codeshare agreement between Air Berlin and Etihad Airways.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> The cooperation of the frequent flyer programs topbonus and Etihad Guest was announced in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> In June 2012, the collaboration concluded with the bonus programs airberlin business points and Ethiad Airways Business Connect for SMBs.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 March 2012, the announced entry into the airline alliance oneworld was officially completed.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> The extended international network offers over 800 destinations in 150 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> At the same time, the airline introduced the Platinum status for its frequent flyer program topbonus.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012 Air Berlin presented its new fare structure "Your Fare" in an effort to offer individual rates for all target groups. Bookings are available for the rates "Just Fly", "Fly Classic" and "FlyFlex" for flights from 1 July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> On 11 May 2012 Air Berlin opened its triweekly non-stop flight from Berlin to Los Angeles in the summer schedule, a destination which until then had only been served from Düsseldorf.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> In March 2013, the Berlin-Chicago route started, feeding into <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>' hub at <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O'Hare International Airport">O'Hare International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 December 2012 Air Berlin announced that <i>topbonus</i>, its frequent flyer program, would be sold to Etihad Airways; only a 30-percent minority share would be retained.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> Air Berlin also announced the expansion of the existing codeshare agreement with Etihad Airways on 20 December 2012. This includes flights via Abu Dhabi to Chengdu, Beijing, Shanghai, Tokyo and Nagoya.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:120513-BER-innen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/120513-BER-innen.JPG/220px-120513-BER-innen.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/120513-BER-innen.JPG/330px-120513-BER-innen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/120513-BER-innen.JPG/440px-120513-BER-innen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2176" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:120513-BER-innen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Air Berlin intends to move its largest hub from Tegel to <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a> <i>(terminal interior pictured)</i>. Originally planned for 2012, the opening of the new airport has been greatly delayed. Currently, it is considered that the airport will not open before late 2017.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 2013, the first Airbus A330-200 was introduced with a new business class which enables a fully flat position for the first time. The long-haul fleet of Air Berlin had already been modified with a business class of high quality in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-business_class_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business_class-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 January 2013 Air Berlin appointed Austrian Wolfgang Prock-Schauer, former Chief Strategy and Planning Officer, as the company's CEO, replacing Hartmut Mehdorn. Mehdorn had held the position on an interim basis since September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the addition of the only connection between Berlin and Chicago from 23 March 2013, Air Berlin uses the Chicago hub for connections within the United States. Air Berlin increased its frequencies to New York-JFK, Los Angeles and Miami, but at the same time cancelled the seasonal non-stop flights to Las Vegas, San Francisco and Vancouver.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2013 Air Berlin announced the closure of its seasonal hub for leisure destinations at <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg Airport</a>. Only ten year-round direct routes remained.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 September 2014, Air Berlin cancelled all remaining 15 orders for their <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787s</a> as well as 18 remaining orders for <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800s</a> as part of their restructuring programme. It is assumed that an all-Airbus fleet is planned.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a> denied Air Berlin authorization to operate 34 routes as a codeshare with co-owner Etihad from the 2014/2015 winter schedule as they would contravene the bilateral traffic rights between Germany and the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Also in October 2014, Air Berlin announced that it was terminating flights to <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a> from both <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Airport" title="Bremen Airport">Bremen Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund_Airport" title="Dortmund Airport">Dortmund Airport</a>, therefore withdrawing entirely from these two German airports.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Air Berlin announced a net loss for 2014 of €376m (€316m loss in 2013). The airline’s revenues in 2014 stagnated at €4.16 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_report_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_report-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, Air Berlin phased out the last <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700s</a> owned by the company. The remaining aircraft of this type will operate on a wetlease basis from <a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> until 2019. All <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-800">Boeing 737-800s</a> are to be phased out by 2016 as Air Berlin plans to focus their short- and medium-haul fleet on the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320 family</a> to cut costs.<sup id="cite_ref-aero.de-737_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aero.de-737-93">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2015, Air Berlin announced the closure of its <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Palma de Mallorca Airport</a> hub by ceasing all Spanish domestic routes by 3 April 2016. It currently serves seven routes within Spain from Palma which are connected to several routes from Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PMIshutdown_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMIshutdown-95">[93]</a></sup> Some days earlier, the airline announced plans to expand its long-haul network with flights from Düsseldorf to Boston, Dallas/Fort Worth, San Francisco and Havana by spring 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> However, the planned route to Dallas/Fort Worth was cancelled a few weeks later due to low demand.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 December 2015, the administrative court in <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig" title="Braunschweig">Braunschweig</a> ruled in favour of the German civil aviation authority (the <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrt-Bundesamt" title="Luftfahrt-Bundesamt">Luftfahrt-Bundesamt</a>) and against Air Berlin regarding some of their codeshare operations with <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>. The shared sale and advertising of 31 out of 83 routes which are marketed by both has been declared illegal and needs to be stopped by 15 January 2016 as it is not covered by the bilateral air traffic agreement between Germany and the UAE. One of the routes which is no longer allowed to use an Etihad codeshare is Air Berlin's service from <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> to <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>. The Luftfahrt-Bundesamt had only allowed these flights until a definite legal ruling was made.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016-2017:_Restructuring_Efforts">2016-2017: Restructuring Efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2016-2017: Restructuring Efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2016, Air Berlin announced a record loss of 446 million euros for 2015. The airline's revenues in 2015 decreased to €4.08 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2015_report_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_report-99">[97]</a></sup> Amongst the reasons considered for Air Berlin's poor performance were: crippling debt of over €800m; unclear and rapid strategy changes on routes and advertising; several <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEOs</a> over recent years; a five-year-plus delay to the new hub <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a>; failed negotiations to profit from lower fuel prices and the overall harsh competition in the airline industry.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelmay_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelmay-100">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2016, Air Berlin confirmed that it no longer owned any of the aircraft it operates, having sold and leased back the last of the aircraft it had previously owned.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> A few weeks later it was reported that Air Berlin and Etihad Airways were in talks with <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> regarding the sale of some of Air Berlin's operational assets to Lufthansa, mainly routes outside of the hubs in Berlin and Düsseldorf, some staff and several aircraft leases.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> Lufthansa is reportedly considering integrating these operations with those of its own <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2016, Air Berlin announced the increase of flights to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> from 55 to 78 nonstops per week for 2017. Besides some frequency increases, Los Angeles and San Francisco will be served from Berlin in addition to the services from Düsseldorf, while Düsseldorf will also see an entirely new route to <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> A few days later, the airline announced the introduction of a business class on its short- and medium-haul flights.<sup id="cite_ref-newbusinessclass_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newbusinessclass-105">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2016, Air Berlin announced that their chief executive <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Pichler" title="Stefan Pichler">Stefan Pichler</a> will step down after serving two years as CEO. He will be replaced February 1 by former head of <a href="/wiki/Germanwings" title="Germanwings">Germanwings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Winkelmann" title="Thomas Winkelmann">Thomas Winkelmann</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span id="Project_&quot;The_new_airberlin&quot;"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_.22The_new_airberlin.22">Project "The new airberlin"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Project &quot;The new airberlin&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 28 September 2016, Air Berlin announced radical restructuring under the project name <i>The new airberlin</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup> The airline will reduce its network from around 140 destinations to 70, and focus on their hubs in Berlin and Düsseldorf, and two smaller bases in Stuttgart and Munich, with six bases being closed.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup> Air Berlin will target business travellers and concentrate on flights to domestic German destinations, Italy, Scandinavia and eastern Europe. It will also expand its long-haul business.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup> The restructuring is also planned to involve the loss of up to 1200 jobs (<a href="/wiki/Full-time_equivalent" title="Full-time equivalent">FTE</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a current narrowbody jet fleet of 118, Air Berlin, including its subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Belair_(airline)" title="Belair (airline)">Belair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>, plans to cut 40 aircraft from the fleet, leaving Air Berlin with its own fleet of 75 aircraft in future, if the deal is approved: 17 Airbus A330-200 for long-haul operations while 40 Airbus A320 family aircraft and 18 Bombardier Q400 aircraft will serve European routes.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> A separate business unit concentrating on tourist destinations will also be formed, with 35 aircraft. This unit might be operated with a new business partner - with <a href="/wiki/TUIfly" class="mw-redirect" title="TUIfly">TUIfly</a> being the assumed partner as they already operate several aircraft for Air Berlin<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> - or sold altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-officialpressrelease_107-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialpressrelease-107">[105]</a></sup> The remaining 40 aircraft including crews are to be wet-leased to competitor <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Lufthansa Group">Lufthansa Group</a> which will use them for their <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> (35 aircraft) and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> (5 aircraft)<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> subsidiaries for a period of six years.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2016, Air Berlin announced plans to close four of its seven <i>airberlin Technik</i> maintenance facilities and lay off 500 of their staff.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-112">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 December 2016, Air Berlin announced plans to sell its entire 49-percent stake in its Austrian subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> to its own minority owner <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nikisale2_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale2-113">[111]</a></sup> Simultaneously, Niki and Air Berlin will exchange several aircraft to harmonize each fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale-5">[5]</a></sup> It has also been announced that Niki will take over several routes to southern European, north African and Turkish leisure destinations from Air Berlin as part of the new joint-venture.<sup id="cite_ref-nikisale2_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikisale2-113">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in December 2016, Air Berlin announced the transfer of its entire fleet of 21 A321-200s to Niki and Niki's transfer of all its 5 A319-100s and 13 A320-200s to Air Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-ch051216_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch051216-114">[112]</a></sup> Air Berlin would discontinue its wet-lease with TUIfly.<sup id="cite_ref-ch051216_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch051216-114">[112]</a></sup> In the same month, it was announced that a total of 38 Airbus A319/A320 aircraft would be wet-leased to Lufthansa Group's Eurowings (33 aircraft) and Austrian Airlines (five), effective February 2017. As a result, lowering Air Berlin's restructuring costs.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2017, Air Berlin announced a network reduction for the upcoming 2017 season, with most leisure routes either transferred to <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a> or cancelled altogether; some domestic and European city routes are to be dropped with the remaining reduced network focusing on the Berlin-Tegel and Düsseldorf hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 28 April 2017, a loss of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a> -781.9 million was announced for 2016, from a revenue of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a> 3.79 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2016_report_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_report-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in late April 2017, Air Berlin confirmed the creation of <i>Air Berlin Aeronautics <a href="/wiki/GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="GmbH">GmbH</a></i>, a new subsidiary which will possess its own operational licence (AOC) to take over the <a href="/wiki/Wetlease" class="mw-redirect" title="Wetlease">wetlease</a> operations currently handled by Air Berlin on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-abaeronautics_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abaeronautics-117">[115]</a></sup> Therefore, the 'actual' Air Berlin will focus on the operations under its own brand name.<sup id="cite_ref-abaeronautics_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abaeronautics-117">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2017, Air Berlin announced it would buy <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtgesellschaft_Walter" title="Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter">Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter</a> entirely, in which it had a controlling stake since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bankruptcy">Bankruptcy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bankruptcy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 15 August 2017, Air Berlin entered insolvency procedures after the withdrawal of ongoing support from its largest shareholder, <a href="/wiki/Etihad" class="mw-redirect" title="Etihad">Etihad</a>, and the resignation of board directors appointed by Etihad.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> By late August 2017, a number of bidders had declared an interest in purchasing parts of the airline, including aircraft and takeoff and landing slots.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> All bidders were given a final deadline of 15 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 September 2017, Air Berlin announced the termination of all flights to the Caribbean by 25 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ABCaribbean_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCaribbean-122">[120]</a></sup> Shortly after, it was made public that leasing company <a href="/wiki/AerCap" title="AerCap">AerCap</a> announced the reposession of ten <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-200">Airbus A330-200s</a> leased to Air Berlin on short notice leading to the termination of several long-haul routes.<sup id="cite_ref-aercap_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aercap-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 September 2017, it was announced that all Air Berlin long-haul flights would end by 15 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-ABlonghaultermination_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABlonghaultermination-124">[122]</a></sup> It has also been announced that the board of Air Berlin intensified talks with <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> and its subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> as the preferred bidders for major parts of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-ABlonghaultermination_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABlonghaultermination-124">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg/220px-Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg/330px-Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg/440px-Air_Berlin_Geb%C3%A4ude_2_Eingang_Buchholzweg_7-8_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="685" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Air Berlin PLC shares are publicly traded on <a href="/wiki/Xetra_(trading_system)" title="Xetra (trading system)">Xetra</a> and on the Frankfurt Stock Exchange in the regulated market. Trading in the regulated unofficial market takes place at the exchanges in Berlin, Düsseldorf, Hamburg, Munich and Stuttgart.<sup id="cite_ref-Report_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report-125">[123]</a></sup> Since December 2011, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> has been the largest shareholder in Air Berlin. As of December 2015, major shareholders (over 5%) are:<sup id="cite_ref-2015_report_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_report-99">[97]</a></sup></p>
<center>
<table class="wikitable" align="center">
<tr>
<th style="background-color:#CC1F2F;;color: white;">Name</th>
<th style="background-color:#CC1F2F;;color: white;width:100px;">Interest</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways PJSC</a></td>
<td align="right">29.21%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>ESAS Holding AS (owners of <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a>)</td>
<td align="right">12.02%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Other shareholders</td>
<td align="right">58.77%</td>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_school">Flight school</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Flight school">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Air Berlin has been running its own pilot-training scheme since 2007 in a joint venture with the TFC Käufer flight school. Trainees complete their commercial pilot training to the latest industry standards over a period of around 24 months. The Air Berlin flight school was the first flight school in Germany to be awarded a training licence by the German Department of Aviation for the new Multi-Crew Pilot Licence concept in February 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_services">Technical services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Technical services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Air Berlin has its own maintenance and overhaul branch, <i>airberlin technik</i> with facilities in Berlin, Düsseldorf, Munich, Stuttgart, Frankfurt, Hamburg and Nuremberg which employs 1300 staff as of October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-112">[110]</a></sup> The technical branch is a certified EASA Part-145 maintenance organization with approximately 1200 employees providing services to both Air Berlin group aircraft and customers throughout Europe. airberlin technik is recognized and approved by various National Airworthiness Authorities such as USA FAA-145, Canadian CAA-145, Aruba EASA-145, Federal Aviation Authority of Russia, GCAA, United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> In October 2016, Air Berlin announced to close the technical bases in Stuttgart, Frankfurt, Hamburg and Nuremberg while laying of 500 staff due to restructuring measures.<sup id="cite_ref-abtechnikshutdown_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abtechnikshutdown-112">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin_destinations" title="Air Berlin destinations">Air Berlin destinations</a></div>
<p>As of October 2017, Air Berlin flies to 42 scheduled year-round and seasonal destinations in 15 countries in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup></p>

<td>operated by <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtgesellschaft_Walter" title="Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter">LGW</a></td>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_fleet">Historical fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Historical fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_F100.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Air_Berlin_F100.jpg/220px-Air_Berlin_F100.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Air_Berlin_F100.jpg/330px-Air_Berlin_F100.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Air_Berlin_F100.jpg/440px-Air_Berlin_F100.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="820" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Berlin_F100.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

Most of them were leased from <a href="/wiki/Germania_(airline)" title="Germania (airline)">Germania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-planespotters_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planespotters-22">[20]</a></sup></div>
