<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_cabins">Aircraft cabins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Aircraft cabins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-111,_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-111%2C_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-111,_Air_Berlin_AN1584645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Air Berlin <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319-100">Airbus A319-100</a> cabin</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-haul_flights">Long-haul flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Long-haul flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Air Berlin long-haul aircraft feature business and economy class sections. At the beginning of 2012, Air Berlin started the renewal of its long-haul cabin, equipping both economy class and business class with new seats and a new in-flight entertainment system. Fully automatic seats that could tilt up to 170 degrees provided high comfort in the business class, in addition to an anti-thrombosis edition and an individually adjustable headrest, and more legroom, narrower seat back, the seat improves comfort in economy class. All seats have an 8.9-inch monitor that is easy to use per touch screen and offers a variety of movies, series, music, audio books and games.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> In January 2013 the airline again presented a new business class which replaced the one introduced a year earlier. Primarily, the new business class has single seats, thus offering travellers even more privacy. The new seats have a full-flat function, a massage function and feature a 15-inch monitor.<sup id="cite_ref-business_class_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-business_class-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Short-_and_medium-haul_flights">Short- and medium-haul flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Short- and medium-haul flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Air Berlin did not offer a Business class product on its short- and medium-haul flights until the airline announced its introduction in August 2016. All short- and medium-haul aircraft will now feature a designated business class in row 1 with expanded services including an empty middle seat.<sup id="cite_ref-newbusinessclass_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newbusinessclass-105">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_services">Passenger services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Passenger services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/220px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/330px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG/440px-Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tegel_airport_02.03.2013_13-10-22.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Air Berlin check-in counters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In contrast to pure European low-cost carriers, Air Berlin offered free in-flight snacks and drinks until September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> Newspapers and magazines are available on domestic German flights.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Full hot meals are complimentary on long-haul flights. On all Air Berlin routes with a flight time of 60 minutes or longer, gourmet meals are offered, which are, according to the airline, created by chefs at "Sansibar", a famous restaurant on the island of <a href="/wiki/Sylt" title="Sylt">Sylt</a>. The airline also offers in-flight entertainment, assigned seating and guaranteed flight connections.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> Air Berlin's basic fares are both nonrefundable and not changeable, so unused flights/fares are a complete loss to the purchaser.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent_flyer_program">Frequent flyer program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Frequent flyer program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Air Berlin's <a href="/wiki/Frequent_flyer_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Frequent flyer program">frequent flyer program</a> is called <i>topbonus</i>. Points, known as miles, can be collected on flights operated by Air Berlin, Niki, Oneworld Alliance airline partners, and selected other airlines. Accrued miles can be redeemed for award flights, or for an upgrade to business class. In addition to the entry-level "topbonus Card Classic" there are cards with Silver, Gold, and Platinum status, corresponding to Oneworld Ruby, Sapphire, and Emerald statuses. A Service Card and a Credit Card, for which a charge is made, are also available.</p>
<p>Ethiad purchased a 70% stake in Top Bonus for €184 million in 2012. Following the insolvency of Air Berlin, Top Bonus also filed for insolvency on 25 August 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Air_Berlin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of August 2016, Air Berlin never suffered an accident or incident resulting in the loss of life or an aircraft in over 35 years of operations. However, there has been recent controversy regarding one of the airline's safety policies:</p>
<ul>
<li>In August 2016, the German aviation authority <a href="/wiki/Luftfahrtbundesamt" class="mw-redirect" title="Luftfahrtbundesamt">Luftfahrtbundesamt</a> criticized Air Berlin for their policy regarding emergency exit seats. As customers need to pay a fee to sit in these rows due to their extended space, Air Berlin regularly leaves the exit rows empty if nobody paid the fee instead of placing randomly selected customers here. The Luftfahrtbundesamt stated that several regulations require someone to be seated there, while Air Berlin said that there are no such rules and in the case of an emergency, the exit could be opened by the first person to reach it.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
